ok {\\n351: \\t\\treturn ParseObjectName(d.Key)\\n352: \\t}\\n353: \\treturn ObjectToName(obj)\\n354: }\\n355: \\n356: // InformerOptions configure a Reflector.\\n357: type InformerOptions struct {\\n358: \\t// ListerWatcher implements List and Watch functions for the source of the resource\\n359: \\t// the informer will be informing about.\\n360: \\tListerWatcher ListerWatcher\\n361: \\n362: \\t// ObjectType is an object of the type that informer is expected to receive.\\n363: \\tObjectType runtime.Object\\n364: \\n365: \\t// Handler defines functions that should called on object mutations.\\n366: \\tHandler ResourceEventHandler\\n367: \\n368: \\t// ResyncPeriod is the underlying Reflector's resync period. If non-zero, the store\\n369: \\t// is re-synced with that frequency - Modify events are delivered even if objects\\n370: \\t// didn't change.\\n371: \\t// This is useful for synchronizing objects that configure external resources\\n372: \\t// (e.g. configure cloud provider functionalities).\\n373: \\t// Optional - if unset, store resyncing is not happening periodically.\\n374: \\tResyncPeriod time.Duration\\n375: \\n376: \\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\\n377: \\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\\n378: \\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\\n379: \\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\\n380: \\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\\n381: \\n382: \\t// Indexers, if set, are the indexers for the received objects to optimize\\n383: \\t// certain queries.\\n384: \\t// Optional - if unset no indexes are maintained.\\n385: \\tIndexers Indexers\\n386: \\n387: \\t// Transform function, if set, will be called on all objects before they will be\\n388: \\t// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will be invoked\\n389: \\t// for them.\\n390: \\t// Optional - if unset no additional transforming is happening.\\n391: \\tTransform TransformFunc\\n392: }\\n393: \\n394: // NewInformerWithOptions returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\\n395: // while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\\n396: // Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\\n397: // notifications to be faulty.\\n398: func NewInformerWithOptions(options InformerOptions) (Store, Controller) {\\n399: \\tvar clientState Store\\n400: \\tif options.Indexers == nil {\\n401: \\t\\tclientState = NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\\n402: \\t} else {\\n403: \\t\\tclientState = NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, options.Indexers)\\n404: \\t}\\n405: \\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\\n406: }\\n407: \\n408: // NewInformer returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\\n409: // while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\\n410: // Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\\n411: // notifications to be faulty.\\n412: //\\n413: // Parameters:\\n414: //   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\\n415: //     be informed of.\\n416: //   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\\n417: //   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\\n418: //     calls, even if nothing changed). Otherwise, re-list will be delayed as\\n419: //     long as possible (until the upstream source closes the watch or times out,\\n420: //     or you stop the controller).\\n421: //   - h is the object you want notifications sent to.\\n422: //\\n423: // Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\\n424: func NewInformer(\\n425: \\tlw ListerWatcher,\\n426: \\tobjType runtime.Object,\\n427: \\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\\n428: \\th ResourceEventHandler,\\n429: ) (Store, Controller) {\\n430: \\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\\n431: \\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\\n432: \\n433: \\toptions := InformerOptions{\\n434: \\t\\tListerWatcher: lw,\\n435: \\t\\tObjectType:    objType,\\n436: \\t\\tHandler:       h,\\n437: \\t\\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\\n438: \\t}\\n439: \\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\\n440: }\\n441: \\n442: // NewIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a Controller for populating the index\\n443: // while also providing event notifications. Such informers, in turn, are key components\n33: // in the high level controllers that form the backbone of the\n34: // Kubernetes control plane.  Look at those for examples, or the\n35: // example in\n36: // https://github.com/kubernetes/client-go/tree/master/examples/workqueue\n37: // .\n38: \n39: // Config contains all the settings for one of these low-level controllers.\n40: type Config struct {\n41: \t// The queue for your objects - has to be a DeltaFIFO due to\n42: \t// assumptions in the implementation. Your Process() function\n43: \t// should accept the output of this Queue's Pop() method.\n44: \tQueue\n45: \n46: \t// Something that can list and watch your objects.\n47: \tListerWatcher\n48: \n49: \t// Something that can process a popped Deltas.\n50: \tProcess ProcessFunc\n51: \n52: \t// ObjectType is an example object of the type this controller is\n53: \t// expected to handle.\n54: \tObjectType runtime.Object\n55: \n56: \t// ObjectDescription is the description to use when logging type-specific information about this controller.\n57: \tObjectDescription string\n58: \n59: \t// FullResyncPeriod is the period at which ShouldResync is considered.\n60: \tFullResyncPeriod time.Duration\n61: \n62: \t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n63: \t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n64: \t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n65: \t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n66: \tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n67: \n68: \t// ShouldResync is periodically used by the reflector to determine\n69: \t// whether to Resync the Queue. If ShouldResync is `nil` or\n70: \t// returns true, it means the reflector should proceed with the\n71: \t// resync.\n72: \tShouldResync ShouldResyncFunc\n73: \n74: \t// If true, when Process() returns an error, re-enqueue the object.\n75: \t// TODO: add interface to let you inject a delay/backoff or drop\n76: \t//       the object completely if desired. Pass the object in\n77: \t//       question to this interface as a parameter.  This is probably moot\n78: \t//       now that this functionality appears at a higher level.\n79: \tRetryOnError bool\n80: \n81: \t// Called whenever the ListAndWatch drops the connection with an error.\n82: \tWatchErrorHandler WatchErrorHandler\n83: \n84: \t// WatchListPageSize is the requested chunk size of initial and relist watch lists.\n85: \tWatchListPageSize int64\n86: }\n87: \n88: // ShouldResyncFunc is a type of function that indicates if a reflector should perform a\n89: // resync or not. It can be used by a shared informer to support multiple event handlers with custom\n90: // resync periods.\n91: type ShouldResyncFunc func() bool\n92: \n93: // ProcessFunc processes a single object.\n94: type ProcessFunc func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) error\n95: \n96: // `*controller` implements Controller\n97: type controller struct {\n98: \tconfig         Config\n99: \treflector      *Reflector\n100: \treflectorMutex sync.RWMutex\n101: \tclock          clock.Clock\n102: }\n103: \n104: // Controller is a low-level controller that is parameterized by a\n105: // Config and used in sharedIndexInformer.\n106: type Controller interface {\n107: \t// Run does two things.  One is to construct and run a Reflector\n108: \t// to pump objects/notifications from the Config's ListerWatcher\n109: \t// to the Config's Queue and possibly invoke the occasional Resync\n110: \t// on that Queue.  The other is to repeatedly Pop from the Queue\n111: \t// and process with the Config's ProcessFunc.  Both of these\n112: \t// continue until `stopCh` is closed.\n113: \tRun(stopCh <-chan struct{})\n114: \n115: \t// HasSynced delegates to the Config's Queue\n116: \tHasSynced() bool\n117: \n118: \t// LastSyncResourceVersion delegates to the Reflector when there\n119: \t// is one, otherwise returns the empty string\n120: \tLastSyncResourceVersion() string\n121: }\n122: \n123: // New makes a new Controller from the given Config.\n124: func New(c *Config) Controller {\n125: \tctlr := &controller{\n126: \t\tconfig: *c,\n127: \t\tclock:  &clock.RealClock{},\n128: \t}\n129: \treturn ctlr\n130: }\n131: \n132: // Run begins processing items, and will continue until a value is sent down stopCh or it is closed.\n133: // It's an error to call Run more than once.\n134: // Run blocks; call via go.\n135: func (c *controller) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n136: \tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrash()\n137: \tgo func() {\n138: \t\t<-stopCh\n139: \t\tc.config.Queue.Close()\n140: \t}()\n141: \tr := NewReflectorWithOptions(\n142: \t\tc.config.ListerWatcher,\n143: \t\tc.config.ObjectType,\n144: \t\tc.config.Queue,\n145: \t\tReflectorOptions{\n146: \t\t\tResyncPeriod:    c.config.FullResyncPeriod,\n147: \t\t\tMinWatchTimeout: c.config.MinWatchTimeout,\n148: \t\t\tTypeDescription: c.config.ObjectDescription,\n149: \t\t\tClock:           c.clock,\n150: \t\t},\n151: \t)\n152: \tr.ShouldResync = c.config.ShouldResync\n153: \tr.WatchListPageSize = c.config.WatchListPageSize\n154: \tif c.config.WatchErrorHandler != nil {\n155: \t\tr.watchErrorHandler = c.config.WatchErrorHandler\n156: \t}\n157: \n158: \tc.reflectorMutex.Lock()\n159: \tc.reflector = r\n160: \tc.reflectorMutex.Unlock()\n161: \n162: \tvar wg wait.Group\n163: \n164: \twg.StartWithChannel(stopCh, r.Run)\n165: \n166: \twait.Until(c.processLoop, time.Second, stopCh)\n167: \twg.Wait()\n168: }\n169: \n170: // Returns true once this controller has completed an initial resource listing\n171: func (c *controller) HasSynced() bool {\n172: \treturn c.config.Queue.HasSynced()\n173: }\n174: \n175: func (c *controller) LastSyncResourceVersion() string {\n176: \tc.reflectorMutex.RLock()\n177: \tdefer c.reflectorMutex.RUnlock()\n178: \tif c.reflector == nil {\n179: \t\treturn \"\"\n180: \t}\n181: \treturn c.reflector.LastSyncResourceVersion()\n182: }\n183: \n184: // processLoop drains the work queue.\n185: // TODO: Consider doing the processing in parallel. This will require a little thought\n186: // to make sure that we don't end up processing the same object multiple times\n187: // concurrently.\n188: //\n189: // TODO: Plumb through the stopCh here (and down to the queue) so that this can\n190: // actually exit when the controller is stopped. Or just give up on this stuff\n191: // ever being stoppable. Converting this whole package to use Context would\n192: // also be helpful.\n193: func (c *controller) processLoop() {\n194: \tfor {\n195: \t\tobj, err := c.config.Queue.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\n196: \t\tif err != nil {\n197: \t\t\tif err == ErrFIFOClosed {\n198: \t\t\t\treturn\n199: \t\t\t}\n200: \t\t\tif c.config.RetryOnError {\n201: \t\t\t\t// This is the safe way to re-enqueue.\n202: \t\t\t\tc.config.Queue.AddIfNotPresent(obj)\n203: \t\t\t}\n204: \t\t}\n205: \t}\n206: }\n207: \n208: // ResourceEventHandler can handle notifications for events that\n209: // happen to a resource. The events are informational only, so you\n210: // can't return an error.  The handlers MUST NOT modify the objects\n211: // received; this concerns not only the top level of structure but all\n212: // the data structures reachable from it.\n213: //   - OnAdd is called when an object is added.\n214: //   - OnUpdate is called when an object is modified. Note that oldObj is the\n215: //     last known state of the object-- it is possible that several changes\n216: //     were combined together, so you can't use this to see every single\n217: //     change. OnUpdate is also called when a re-list happens, and it will\n218: //     get called even if nothing changed. This is useful for periodically\n219: //     evaluating or syncing something.\n220: //   - OnDelete will get the final state of the item if it is known, otherwise\n221: //     it will get an object of type DeletedFinalStateUnknown. This can\n222: //     happen if the watch is closed and misses the delete event and we don't\n223: //     notice the deletion until the subsequent re-list.\n224: type ResourceEventHandler interface {\n225: \tOnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n226: \tOnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n227: \tOnDelete(obj interface{})\n228: }\n229: \n230: // ResourceEventHandlerFuncs is an adaptor to let you easily specify as many or\n231: // as few of the notification functions as you want while still implementing\n232: // ResourceEventHandler.  This adapter does not remove the prohibition against\n233: // modifying the objects.\n234: //\n235: // See ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs if your use needs to propagate\n236: // HasSynced.\n237: type ResourceEventHandlerFuncs struct {\n238: \tAddFunc    func(obj interface{})\n239: \tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n240: \tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n241: }\n242: \n243: // OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\n244: func (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n245: \tif r.AddFunc != nil {\n246: \t\tr.AddFunc(obj)\n247: \t}\n248: }\n249: \n250: // OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\n251: func (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n252: \tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n253: \t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n254: \t}\n255: }\n256: \n257: // OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\n258: func (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n259: \tif An object\n296: // that starts passing the filter after an update is considered an add, and an\n297: // object that stops passing the filter after an update is considered a delete.\n298: // Like the handlers, the filter MUST NOT modify the objects it is given.\n299: type FilteringResourceEventHandler struct {\n300: \tFilterFunc func(obj interface{}) bool\n301: \tHandler    ResourceEventHandler\n302: }\n303: \n304: // OnAdd calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\n305: func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n306: \tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n307: \t\treturn\n308: \t}\n309: \tr.Handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n310: }\n311: \n312: // OnUpdate ensures the proper handler is called depending on whether the filter matches\n313: func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n314: \tnewer := r.FilterFunc(newObj)\n315: \tolder := r.FilterFunc(oldObj)\n316: \tswitch {\n317: \tcase newer && older:\n318: \t\tr.Handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\n319: \tcase newer && !older:\n320: \t\tr.Handler.OnAdd(newObj, false)\n321: \tcase !newer && older:\n322: \t\tr.Handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\n323: \tdefault:\n324: \t\t// do nothing\n325: \t}\n326: }\n327: \n328: // OnDelete calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\n329: func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n330: \tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n331: \t\treturn\n332: \t}\n333: \tr.Handler.OnDelete(obj)\n334: }\n335: \n336: // DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc checks for\n337: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n338: // MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n339: func DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj interface{}) (string, error) {\n340: \tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); nil\\n606: }\\n607: \\n608: // watchList establishes a stream to get a consistent snapshot of data\\n609: // from the server as described in https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/tree/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/3157-watch-list#proposal\\n610: //\\n611: // case 1: start at Most Recent (RV=\\\"\\\", ResourceVersionMatch=ResourceVersionMatchNotOlderThan)\\n612: // Establishes a consistent stream with the server.\\n613: // That means the returned data is consistent, as if, served directly from etcd via a quorum read.\\n614: // It begins with synthetic \\\"Added\\\" events of all resources up to the most recent ResourceVersion.\\n615: // It ends with a synthetic \\\"Bookmark\\\" event containing the most recent ResourceVersion.\\n616: // After receiving a \\\"Bookmark\\\" event the reflector is considered to be synchronized.\\n617: // It replaces its internal store with the collected items and\\n618: // reuses the current watch requests for getting further events.\\n619: //\\n620: // case 2: start at Exact (RV>\\\"0\\\", ResourceVersionMatch=ResourceVersionMatchNotOlderThan)\\n621: // Establishes a stream with the server at the provided resource version.\\n622: // To establish the initial state the server begins with synthetic \\\"Added\\\" events.\\n623: // It ends with a synthetic \\\"Bookmark\\\" event containing the provided or newer resource version.\\n624: // After receiving a \\\"Bookmark\\\" event the reflector is considered to be synchronized.\\n625: // It replaces its internal store with the collected items and\\n626: // reuses the current watch requests for getting further events.\\n627: func (r *Reflector) watchList(stopCh <-chan struct{}) (watch.Interface, error) {\\n628: \\tvar w watch.Interface\\n629: \\tvar err error\\n630: \\tvar temporaryStore Store\\n631: \\tvar resourceVersion string\\n632: \\t// TODO(#115478): see if this \\t\\t\\t<-r.backoffManager.Backoff().C()\\n639: \\t\\t\\treturn true\\n640: \\t\\t}\\n641: \\t\\tif isExpiredError(err) || isTooLargeResourceVersionError(err) {\\n642: \\t\\t\\t// we tried to data\n101: \t// (RV=\"0\") it will default to pager.PageSize, for the rest (RV != \"\" && RV != \"0\")\n102: \t// it will turn off pagination to allow serving them from watch cache.\n103: \t// NOTE: This enables you to use reflectors to periodically process\n223: // everything as well as incrementally processing the things that\n224: // change.\n225: func NewReflectorWithOptions(lw ListerWatcher, expectedType interface{}, store Store, options ReflectorOptions) *Reflector {\n226: \treflectorClock := options.Clock\n227: \tif reflectorClock == nil {\n228: \t\treflectorClock = clock.RealClock{}\n229: \t}\n230: \tminWatchTimeout := defaultMinWatchTimeout\n231: \tif options.MinWatchTimeout > defaultMinWatchTimeout {\n232: \t\tminWatchTimeout = options.MinWatchTimeout\n233: \t}\n234: \tr := &Reflector{\n235: \t\tname:            options.Name,\n236: \t\tresyncPeriod:    options.ResyncPeriod,\n237: \t\tminWatchTimeout: minWatchTimeout,\n238: \t\ttypeDescription: options.TypeDescription,\n239: \t\tlisterWatcher:   lw,\n240: \t\tstore:           store,\n241: \t\t// We used to make the call every 1sec (1 QPS), the goal here is to achieve ~98% traffic reduction when\n242: \t\t// API server is not healthy. With these parameters, backoff will stop at [30,60) sec interval which is\n243: \t\t// 0.22 QPS. If we don't backoff for 2min, assume API server is healthy and we reset the backoff.\n244: \t\tbackoffManager:    wait.NewExponentialBackoffManager(800*time.Millisecond, 30*time.Second, 2*time.Minute, 2.0, 1.0, reflectorClock),\n245: \t\tclock:             reflectorClock,\n246: \t\twatchErrorHandler: WatchErrorHandler(DefaultWatchErrorHandler),\n247: \t\texpectedType:      reflect.TypeOf(expectedType),\n248: \t}\n249: \n250: \tif r.name == \"\" {\n251: \t\tr.name = naming.GetNameFromCallsite(internalPackages...)\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \tif r.typeDescription == \"\" \t}\n261: \n262: \t// don't overwrite UseWatchList if already set\n263: \t// because the higher layers (e.g. storage/cacher) disabled it on purpose\n264: \tif r.UseWatchList == nil {\n265: }\n344: \n345: // ListAndWatch first lists all items and get the resource version at the moment of call,\n346: // and then use the resource version to watch.\n347: // It returns error if ListAndWatch didn't even try to initialize watch.\n348: func (r *Reflector) ListAndWatch(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error {\n349: \tklog.V(3).Infof(\"Listing and watching %v from %s\", r.typeDescription, r.name)\n350: \tvar err error\n351: \tvar w watch.Interface\n352: \tuseWatchList := ptr.Deref(r.UseWatchList, false)\n353: \tfallbackToList := !useWatchList\n354: \n355: \tif useWatchList {\n356: server.\n418: func (r *Reflector) watch(w watch.Interface, stopCh <-chan struct{}, resyncerrc chan error) error {\n419: \tvar err error\n420: \tretry := NewRetryWithDeadline(r.MaxInternalErrorRetryDuration, time.Minute, apierrors.IsInternalError, r.clock)\n421: \n422: \tfor {\n423: \t\t// give the stopCh a chance to stop the loop, even in case of \t\t}\n465: \n466: \t\terr = handleWatch(start, w, r.store, r.expectedType, r.expectedGVK, r.name, r.typeDescription, r.setLastSyncResourceVersion,\n467: \t\t\tr.clock, resyncerrc, stopCh)\n468: consistent snapshot of data\n609: // from the server as described in https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/tree/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/3157-watch-list#proposal\n610: //\n611: // case 1: start at Most Recent (RV=\"\", ResourceVersionMatch=ResourceVersionMatchNotOlderThan)\n612: // Establishes a consistent stream with the server.\n613: // That means the returned data is consistent, as \"Bookmark\" event containing the most recent ResourceVersion.\n616: // After receiving a \"Bookmark\" event the reflector is considered to be synchronized.\n617: // It replaces its internal store with the collected items and\n618: // reuses the current watch requests for getting further events.\n619: //\n620: // case 2: start at Exact (RV>\"0\", earlier, the api server returns both apierrors.StatusReasonExpired and\n942: \t// apierrors.StatusReasonGone for HTTP 410 (Gone) status code responses. In 1.18 the kube server is more consistent\n943: \t// and always returns apierrors.StatusReasonExpired. For backward compatibility we can only remove the apierrors.IsGone\n944: \t// check when we fully drop support for Kubernetes 1.17 servers from reflectors.\n945: \treturn apierrors.IsResourceExpired(err) || apierrors.IsGone(err)\n946: }\n947: \n948: func isTooLargeResourceVersionError(err error) bool {\n949: \tif apierrors.HasStatusCause(err, metav1.CauseTypeResourceVersionTooLarge) {\n950: \t\treturn true\n951: \t}\n952: \t// In Kubernetes 1.17.0-1.18.5, the api server doesn't set the error status cause to\n953: \t// metav1.CauseTypeResourceVersionTooLarge to indicate that the requested minimum resource\n954: \t// version is larger than the largest currently available resource version. {\n958: \t\treturn false\n959: \t}\n960: \tapierr, ok := err.(apierrors.APIStatus)\n961: \tif !ok || apierr == nil || apierr.Status().Details == nil {\n962: \t\treturn false\n963: \t}\n964: \tfor _, cause := range apierr.Status().Details.Causes {\n965: \t\t// Matches the message returned by api server 1.17.0-1.18.5 for this error condition\n966: \t\tif cause.Message == \"Too large resource All are\\n32: // optional.\\n33: type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\\n34: \\n35: \\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\\n36: \\t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\\n37: \\t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\\n38: \\t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\\n39: \\tKeyFunction KeyFunc\\n40: \\n41: \\t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\\n42: \\t// this queue \\\"knows about\\\". It is used to decide which items are missing\\n43: \\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\\n44: \\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\\n45: \\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\\n46: \\n47: \\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\\n48: \\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\\n49: \\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\\n50: \\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\\n51: \\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\\n52: \\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\\n53: \\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n54: \\n55: \\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\\n56: \\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\\n57: \\tTransformer TransformFunc\\n58: }\\n59: \\n60: // DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\\n69: //\\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\\n74: // resync events.\\n75: //\\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\\n78: // the Pop() method.\\n79: //\\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\\n86: //\\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\\n90: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\\n91: //\\n92: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\\n93: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\\n94: // question are called \\\"known objects\\\" and this set of objects\\n95: // modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\\n96: // (each in a different way).\\n97: //\\n98: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\\n99: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\\n100: // different versions of the same object.\\n101: type DeltaFIFO struct {\\n102: \\t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\\n103: \\tlock sync.RWMutex\\n104: \\tcond sync.Cond\\n105: \\n106: \\t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\\n107: \\t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\\n108: \\titems map[string]Deltas\\n109: \\n110: \\t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\\n111: \\t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\\n112: \\t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\\n113: \\tqueue []string\\n114: \\n115: \\t// populated is true if the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has been populated\\n116: \\t// or Delete/Add/Update/AddIfNotPresent was called first.\\n117: \\tpopulated bool\\n118: \\t// initialPopulationCount is the number of items inserted by the first call of Replace()\\n119: \\tinitialPopulationCount int\\n120: \\n121: \\t// keyFunc is used to make the key used for queued item\\n122: \\t// insertion and retrieval, and should be deterministic.\\n123: \\tkeyFunc KeyFunc\\n124: \\n125: \\t// knownObjects list keys that are \\\"known\\\" --- affecting Delete(),\\n126: \\t// Replace(), and Resync()\\n127: \\tknownObjects KeyListerGetter\\n128: \\n129: \\t// Used to indicate a queue is closed so a control loop can exit when a queue is empty.\\n130: \\t// Currently, not used to gate any of CRUD operations.\\n131: \\tclosed bool\\n132: \\n133: \\t// emitDeltaTypeReplaced is whether to emit the Replaced or Sync\\n134: \\t// DeltaType when Replace() is called (to preserve backwards compat).\\n135: \\temitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n136: \\n137: \\t// Called with every object if non-nil.\\n138: \\ttransformer TransformFunc\\n139: }\\n140: \\n141: // TransformFunc allows for transforming an object before it will be processed.\\n142: //\\n143: // The most common usage pattern is to clean-up some parts of the object to\\n144: // reduce component memory usage if a given component doesn't care about them.\\n145: //\\n146: // New in v1.27: TransformFunc sees the object before any other actor, and it\\n147: // is now safe to mutate the object in place instead of making a copy.\\n148: //\\n149: // It's recommended for the TransformFunc to be idempotent.\\n150: // It MUST be idempotent if objects already present in the cache are passed to\\n151: // the Replace() to avoid re-mutating them. Default informers do not pass\\n152: // existing objects to Replace though.\\n153: //\\n154: // Note that TransformFunc is called while inserting objects into the\\n155: // notification queue and is therefore extremely performance sensitive; please\\n156: // do not do anything that will take a long time.\\n157: type TransformFunc func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)\\n158: \\n159: // DeltaType is the type of a change (addition, deletion, etc)\\n160: type DeltaType string\\n161: \\n162: // Change type definition\\n163: const (\\n164: \\tAdded   DeltaType = \\\"Added\\\"\\n165: \\tUpdated DeltaType = \\\"Updated\\\"\\n166: \\tDeleted DeltaType = \\\"Deleted\\\"\\n167: \\t// Replaced is emitted when we encountered watch errors and had to do a\\n168: \\t// relist. We don't know if the replaced object has changed.\\n169: \\t//\\n170: \\t// NOTE: Previous versions of DeltaFIFO would use Sync for Replace events\\n171: \\t// as well. It tells you what\\n180: // change happened, and the object's state after* that change.\\n181: //\\n182: // [*] Unless the change is a deletion, and then you'll get the final\\n183: // state of the object before it was deleted.\\n184: type Delta struct {\\n185: \\tType   DeltaType\\n186: \\tObject interface{}\\n187: }\\n188: \\n189: // Deltas is a list of one or more 'Delta's to an individual object.\\n190: // The oldest delta is at index 0, the newest delta is the last one.\\n191: type Deltas []Delta\\n192: \\n193: // NewDeltaFIFO returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to items.\\n194: //\\n195: // keyFunc is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It is\\n196: // exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional handling\\n197: // around deleted objects and queue state).\\n198: //\\n199: // 'knownObjects' may be supplied to modify the behavior of Delete,\\n200: // Replace, and Resync.  It may be nil if you do not need those\\n201: // modifications.\\n202: //\\n203: // TODO: consider merging keyLister with this object, tracking a list of\\n204: // \\\"known\\\" keys when Pop() is called. Have to think about how that\\n205: // affects error retrying.\\n206: //\\n207: //\\tNOTE: It is possible to misuse this and cause a race when using an\\n208: //\\texternal known object source.\\n209: //\\tWhether there is a potential race depends on how the consumer\\n210: //\\tmodifies knownObjects. In Pop(), process function is called under\\n211: //\\tlock, so it is safe to update data structures in it that need to be\\n212: //\\tin sync with the queue (e.g. knownObjects).\\n213: //\\n214: //\\tExample:\\n215: //\\tIn case of sharedIndexInformer being a consumer\\n216: //\\t(https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/0cdd940f/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go#L192),\\n217: //\\tthere is no race as knownObjects (s.indexer) is modified safely\\n218: //\\tunder DeltaFIFO's lock. The only exceptions are GetStore() and\\n219: //\\tGetIndexer() methods, which expose ways to modify the underlying\\n220: //\\tstorage. Currently these two methods are used for creating Lister\\n221: //\\tand internal tests.\\n222: //\\n223: // Also see the comment on DeltaFIFO.\\n224: //\\n225: // Warning: This constructs a DeltaFIFO that does not differentiate between\\n226: // events caused by a call to Replace (e.g., from a relist, which may\\n227: // contain object updates), and synthetic events caused by a periodic resync\\n228: // (which just emit the existing object). See https://issue.k8s.io/86015 for details.\\n229: //\\n230: // Use `NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{..., EmitDeltaTypeReplaced: true})`\\n231: // instead to receive a `Replaced` event depending on the type.\\n232: //\\n233: // Deprecated: Equivalent to NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{KeyFunction: keyFunc, KnownObjects: knownObjects})\\n234: func NewDeltaFIFO(keyFunc KeyFunc, knownObjects KeyListerGetter) *DeltaFIFO {\\n235: \\treturn NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{\\n236: \\t\\tKeyFunction:  keyFunc,\\n237: \\t\\tKnownObjects: knownObjects,\\n238: \\t})\\n239: }\\n240: \\n241: // NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to\\n242: // items. See also the comment on DeltaFIFO.\\n243: func NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(opts DeltaFIFOOptions) *DeltaFIFO {\\n244: \\tif opts.KeyFunction == nil {\\n245: \\t\\topts.KeyFunction = MetaNamespaceKeyFunc\\n246: \\t}\\n247: \\n248: \\tf := &DeltaFIFO{\\n249: \\t\\titems:        map[string]Deltas{},\\n250: \\t\\tqueue:        []string{},\\n251: \\t\\tkeyFunc:      opts.KeyFunction,\\n252: \\t\\tknownObjects: opts.KnownObjects,\\n253: \\n254: \\t\\temitDeltaTypeReplaced: opts.EmitDeltaTypeReplaced,\\n255: \\t\\ttransformer:           opts.Transformer,\\n256: \\t}\\n257: \\tf.cond.L = &f.lock\\n258: \\treturn f\\n259: }\\n260: \\n261: var (\\n262: \\t_ = Queue(&DeltaFIFO{}) // DeltaFIFO is a Queue\\n263: )\\n264: \\n265: var (\\n266: \\t// ErrZeroLengthDeltasObject is returned in a KeyError if a Deltas\\n267: \\t// object with zero length is encountered (should be impossible,\\n268: \\t// but included for completeness).\\n269: \\tErrZeroLengthDeltasObject = errors.New(\\\"0 length Deltas object; ok {\\n284: \\t\\tif len(d) == 0 {\\n285: \\t\\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", KeyError{obj, ErrZeroLengthDeltasObject}\\n286: \\t\\t}\\n287: \\t\\tobj = d.Newest().Object\\n288: \\t}\\n289: \\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); The item is only enqueued\\n308: // if it doesn't already exist in the set.\\n309: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Add(obj interface{}) error {\\n310: \\tf.lock.Lock()\\n311: \\tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\\n312: \\tf.populated = true\\n313: \\treturn f.queueActionLocked(Added, obj)\\n314: }\\n315: \\n316: // Update is just like Add, but makes an Updated Delta.\\n317: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Update(obj interface{}) error {\\n318: \\tf.lock.Lock()\\n319: \\tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\\n320: \\tf.populated = true\\n321: \\treturn f.queueActionLocked(Updated, obj)\\n322: }\\n323: \\n324: // Delete is just like Add, but makes a Deleted Delta. If the given\\n325: // object does not already exist, it will be ignored. (It may have\\n326: // already been deleted by a Replace (re-list), for example.)  In this\\n327: // method `f.knownObjects`, if not nil, provides (via GetByKey)\\n328: // _additional_ objects that are considered to already exist.\\n329: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Delete(obj interface{}) error {\\n330: \\tid, err := f.KeyOf(obj)\\n331: \\tif err != nil {\\n332: \\t\\treturn KeyError{obj, err}\\n333: \\t}\\n334: \\tf.lock.Lock()\\n335: \\tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\\n336: \\tf.populated = true\\n337: \\tif f.knownObjects == nil {\\n338: \\t\\tif _, exists := f.items[id]; !exists {\\n339: \\t\\t\\t// Presumably, this was deleted when a relist happened.\\n340: \\t\\t\\t// Don't provide a second report of the same deletion.\\n341: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n342: \\t\\t}\\n343: \\t} else {\\n344: \\t\\t// We only want to skip the \\\"deletion\\\" action if the object doesn't\\n345: \\t\\t// exist in knownObjects and it doesn't have corresponding item in items.\\n346: \\t\\t// Note that even if there is a \\\"deletion\\\" action in items, we can ignore it,\\n347: \\t\\t// because it will be deduped automatically in \\\"queueActionLocked\\\"\\n348: \\t\\t_, exists, err := f.knownObjects.GetByKey(id)\\n349: \\t\\t_, itemsExist := f.items[id]\\n350: \\t\\tif err == nil && !exists && !itemsExist {\\n351: \\t\\t\\t// Presumably, this was deleted when a relist happened.\\n352: \\t\\t\\t// Don't provide a second report of the same deletion.\\n353: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n354: \\t\\t}\\n355: \\t}\\n356: \\n357: \\t// exist in items and/or KnownObjects\\n358: \\treturn f.queueActionLocked(Deleted, obj)\\n359: }\\n360: \\n361: // AddIfNotPresent inserts an item, and puts it in the queue. If the item is already\\n362: // present in the set, it is neither enqueued nor added to the set.\\n363: //\\n364: // This is useful in a single producer/consumer scenario so that the consumer can\\n365: // safely retry items without contending with the producer and potentially enqueueing\\n366: // stale items.\\n367: //\\n368: // Important: obj must be a Deltas (the output of the Pop() function). Yes, this is\\n369: // different from the Add/Update/Delete functions.\\n370: func (f *DeltaFIFO) AddIfNotPresent(obj interface{}) error {\\n371: \\tdeltas, ok := obj.(Deltas)\\n372: \\tif !ok {\\n373: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"object must be of type deltas, but got: %#v\\\", obj)\\n374: \\t}\\n375: \\tid, err := f.KeyOf(deltas)\\n376: \\tif err != nil {\\n377: \\t\\treturn KeyError{obj, err}\\n378: \\t}\\n379: \\tf.lock.Lock()\\n380: \\tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\\n381: \\tf.addIfNotPresent(id, deltas)\\n382: \\treturn nil\\n383: }\\n384: \\n385: // addIfNotPresent inserts deltas under id if it does not exist, and assumes the caller\\n386: // already holds the fifo lock.\\n387: func (f *DeltaFIFO) addIfNotPresent(id string, deltas Deltas) {\\n388: \\tf.populated = true\\n389: \\tif _, exists := f.items[id]; exists {\\n390: \\t\\treturn\\n391: \\t}\\n392: \\n393: \\tf.queue = append(f.queue, id)\\n394: \\tf.items[id] = deltas\\n395: \\tf.cond.Broadcast()\\n396: }\\n397: \\n398: // re-listing and watching can deliver the same update multiple times in any\\n399: // order. This will combine the most recent two deltas if they are the same.\\n400: func dedupDeltas(deltas Deltas) Deltas {\\n401: \\tn := len(deltas)\\n402: \\tif n < 2 {\\n403: \\t\\treturn deltas\\n404: \\t}\\n405: \\ta := &deltas[n-1]\\n406: \\tb := &deltas[n-2]\\n407: \\tif out := isDup(a, b); out != nil {\\n408: \\t\\tdeltas[n-2] = *out\\n409: \\t\\treturn deltas[:n-1]\\n410: \\t}\\n411: \\treturn deltas\\n412: }\\n413: \\n414: // If a & b represent the same event, returns the delta that ought to be kept.\\n415: // Otherwise, returns nil.\\n416: // TODO: is there anything other than deletions that need deduping?\\n417: func isDup(a, b *Delta) *Delta {\\n418: \\tif out := isDeletionDup(a, b); out != nil {\\n419: \\t\\treturn out\\n420: \\t}\\n421: \\t// TODO: Detect other duplicate situations? Are there any?\\n422: \\treturn nil\\n423: }\\n424: \\n425: // keep the one with the most information if both are deletions.\\n426: func isDeletionDup(a, b *Delta) *Delta {\\n427: \\tif b.Type != {\\n432: \\t\\treturn a\\n433: \\t}\\n434: \\treturn b\\n435: }\\n436: \\n437: // queueActionLocked appends to the delta list for the object.\\n438: // Caller must lock first.\\n439: func (f \\t\\\"time\\\"\\n24: \\n25: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/sets\\\"\\n26: \\n27: \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n28: \\tutiltrace \\\"k8s.io/utils/trace\\\"\\n29: )\\n30: \\n31: // DeltaFIFOOptions is the configuration parameters for DeltaFIFO. All are\\n32: // optional.\\n33: type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\\n34: \\n35: \\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\\n36: \\t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\\n37: \\t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\\n38: \\t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\\n39: \\tKeyFunction KeyFunc\\n40: \\n41: \\t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\\n42: \\t// this queue \\\"knows about\\\". It is used to decide which items are missing\\n43: \\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\\n44: \\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\\n45: \\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\\n46: \\n47: \\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\\n48: \\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\\n49: \\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\\n50: \\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\\n51: \\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\\n52: \\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\\n53: \\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n54: \\n55: \\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\\n56: \\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\\n57: \\tTransformer TransformFunc\\n58: }\\n59: \\n60: // DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\\n69: //\\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\\n74: // resync events.\\n75: //\\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\\n78: // the Pop() method.\\n79: //\\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\\n86: //\\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\\n90: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\\n91: //\\n92: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\\n93: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\\n94: // question are called \\\"known objects\\\" and this set of objects\\n95: // modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\\n96: // (each in a different way).\\n97: //\\n98: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\\n99: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\\n100: // different versions of the same object.\\n101: type DeltaFIFO struct {\\n102: \\t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\\n103: \\tlock sync.RWMutex\\n104: \\tcond sync.Cond\\n105: \\n106: \\t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\\n107: \\t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\\n108: \\titems map[string]Deltas\\n109: \\n110: \\t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\\n111: \\t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\\n112: \\t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\\n113: \\tqueue []string\\n114: \\n115: \\t// populated is true if the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has been populated\\n116: \\t// or Delete/Add/Update/AddIfNotPresent was called first.\\n117: \\tpopulated bool\\n118: \\t// initialPopulationCount is the number of items inserted by the first call of Replace()\\n119: \\tinitialPopulationCount int\\n120: \\n121: \\t// keyFunc is used to make the key used for queued item\\n122: \\t// insertion and retrieval, and should be deterministic.\\n123: \\tkeyFunc KeyFunc\\n124: \\n125: \\t// knownObjects list keys that are \\\"known\\\" --- affecting Delete(),\\n126: \\t// Replace(), and Resync()\\n127: \\tknownObjects KeyListerGetter\\n128: \\n129: \\t// Used to indicate a queue is closed so a control loop can exit when a queue is empty.\\n130: \\t// Currently, not used to gate any of CRUD operations.\\n131: \\tclosed bool\\n132: \\n133: \\t// emitDeltaTypeReplaced is whether to emit the Replaced or Sync\\n134: \\t// DeltaType when Replace() is called (to preserve backwards compat).\\n135: \\temitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n136: \\n137: \\t// Called with every object if non-nil.\\n138: \\ttransformer TransformFunc\\n139: }\\n140: \\n141: // TransformFunc allows for transforming an object before it will be processed.\\n142: //\\n143: // The most common usage pattern is to clean-up some parts of the object to\\n144: // reduce component memory usage if a given component doesn't care about them.\\n145: //\\n146: // New in v1.27: TransformFunc sees the object before any other actor, and it\\n147: // is now safe to mutate the object in place instead of making a copy.\\n148: //\\n149: // It's recommended for the TransformFunc to be idempotent.\\n150: // It MUST be idempotent if objects already present in the cache are passed to\\n151: // the Replace() to avoid re-mutating them. Default informers do not pass\\n152: // existing objects to Replace though.\\n153: //\\n154: // Note that TransformFunc is called while inserting objects into the\\n155: // notification queue and is therefore extremely performance sensitive; please\\n156: // do not do anything that will take a long time.\\n157: type TransformFunc func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)\\n158: \\n159: // DeltaType is the type of a change (addition, deletion, etc)\\n160: type DeltaType string\\n161: \\n162: // Change type definition\\n163: const (\\n164: \\tAdded   DeltaType = \\\"Added\\\"\\n165: \\tUpdated DeltaType = \\\"Updated\\\"\\n166: \\tDeleted DeltaType = \\\"Deleted\\\"\\n167: \\t// Replaced is emitted when we encountered watch errors and had to do a\\n168: \\t// relist. We don't know if the replaced object has changed.\\n169: \\t//\\n170: \\t// NOTE: Previous versions of DeltaFIFO would use Sync for Replace events\\n171: \\t// as well. Hence, Replaced is only emitted when the option\\n172: \\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is true.\\n173: \\tReplaced DeltaType = \\\"Replaced\\\"\\n174: \\t// Sync is for synthetic events during a periodic resync.\\n175: \\tSync DeltaType = \\\"Sync\\\"\\n176: )\\n177: \\n178: // Delta is a member of Deltas (a list of Delta objects) which\\n179: // in its turn is the type stored by a DeltaFIFO. It tells you what\\n180: // change happened, and the object's state after* that change.\\n181: //\\n182: // [*] Unless the change is a deletion, and then you'll get the final\\n183: // state of the object before it was deleted.\\n184: type Delta struct {\\n185: \\tType   DeltaType\\n186: \\tObject interface{}\\n187: }\\n188: \\n189: // Deltas is a list of one or more 'Delta's to an individual object.\\n190: // The oldest delta is at index 0, the newest delta is the last one.\\n191: type Deltas []Delta\\n192: \\n193: // NewDeltaFIFO returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to items.\\n194: //\\n195: // keyFunc is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It is\\n196: // exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional handling\\n197: // around deleted objects and queue state).\\n198: //\\n199: // 'knownObjects' may be supplied to modify the behavior of Delete,\\n200: // Replace, and Resync.  It may be nil if you do not need those\\n201: // modifications.\\n202: //\\n203: // TODO: consider merging keyLister with this object, tracking a list of\\n204: // \\\"known\\\" keys when Pop() is called. Have to think about how that\\n205: // affects error retrying.\\n206: //\\n207: //\\tNOTE: It is possible to misuse this and cause a race when using an\\n208: //\\texternal known object source.\\n209: //\\tWhether there is a potential race depends on how the consumer\\n210: //\\tmodifies knownObjects. In Pop(), process function is called under\\n211: //\\tlock, so it is safe to update data structures in it that need to be\\n212: //\\tin sync with the queue (e.g. knownObjects).\\n213: //\\n214: //\\tExample:\\n215: //\\tIn case of sharedIndexInformer being a consumer\\n216: //\\t(https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/0cdd940f/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go#L192),\\n217: //\\tthere is no race as knownObjects (s.indexer) is modified safely\\n218: //\\tunder DeltaFIFO's lock. Currently these two methods are used for creating Lister\\n221: //\\tand internal tests.\\n222: //\\n223: // Also see the comment on DeltaFIFO.\\n224: //\\n225: // Warning: This constructs a DeltaFIFO that does not differentiate between\\n226: // events caused by a call to Replace (e.g., from a relist, which may\\n227: // contain object updates), and synthetic events caused by a periodic resync\\n228: // (which just emit the existing object). See https://issue.k8s.io/86015 for details.\\n229: //\\n230: // Use `NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{..., EmitDeltaTypeReplaced: true})`\\n231: // instead to receive a `Replaced` event depending on the type.\\n232: //\\n233: // Deprecated: Equivalent to NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{KeyFunction: keyFunc, KnownObjects: knownObjects})\\n234: func NewDeltaFIFO(keyFunc KeyFunc, knownObjects KeyListerGetter) *DeltaFIFO {\\n235: \\treturn NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{\\n236: \\t\\tKeyFunction:  keyFunc,\\n237: \\t\\tKnownObjects: knownObjects,\\n238: \\t})\\n239: }\\n240: \\n241: // NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to\\n242: // items. The item is only enqueued\\n308: // if it doesn't already exist in the set.\\n309: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Add(obj interface{}) error {\\n310: \\tf.lock.Lock()\\n311: \\tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\\n312: \\tf.populated = true\\n313: \\treturn f.queueActionLocked(Added, obj)\\n314: }\\n315: \\n316: // Update is just like Add, but makes an Updated Delta.\\n317: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Update(obj interface{}) error {\\n318: \\tf.lock.Lock()\\n319: \\tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\\n320: \\tf.populated = true\\n321: \\treturn f.queueActionLocked(Updated, obj)\\n322: }\\n323: \\n324: // Delete is just like Add, but makes a Deleted Delta. If the given\\n325: // object does not already exist, it will be ignored. (It may have\\n326: // already been deleted by a Replace (re-list), for example.)  In this\\n327: // method `f.knownObjects`, if not nil, provides (via GetByKey)\\n328: // _additional_ objects that are considered to already exist.\\n329: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Delete(obj interface{}) error {\\n330: \\tid, err := f.KeyOf(obj)\\n331: \\tif err != nil {\\n332: \\t\\treturn KeyError{obj, err}\\n333: \\t}\\n334: \\tf.lock.Lock()\\n335: \\tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\\n336: \\tf.populated = true\\n337: \\tif f.knownObjects == nil {\\n338: \\t\\tif _, exists := f.items[id]; !exists {\\n339: \\t\\t\\t// Presumably, this was deleted when a relist happened.\\n340: \\t\\t\\t// Don't provide a second report of the same deletion.\\n341: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n342: \\t\\t}\\n343: \\t} else {\\n344: \\t\\t// We only want to skip the \\\"deletion\\\" action if the object doesn't\\n345: \\t\\t// exist in knownObjects and it doesn't have corresponding item in items.\\n346: \\t\\t// Note that even if there is a \\\"deletion\\\" action in items, we can ignore it,\\n347: \\t\\t// because it will be deduped automatically in \\\"queueActionLocked\\\"\\n348: \\t\\t_, exists, err := f.knownObjects.GetByKey(id)\\n349: \\t\\t_, itemsExist := f.items[id]\\n350: \\t\\tif err == nil && !exists && !itemsExist {\\n351: \\t\\t\\t// Presumably, this was deleted when a relist happened.\\n352: \\t\\t\\t// Don't provide a second report of the same deletion.\\n353: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n354: \\t\\t}\\n355: \\t}\\n356: \\n357: \\t// exist in items and/or KnownObjects\\n358: \\treturn f.queueActionLocked(Deleted, obj)\\n359: }\\n360: \\n361: // AddIfNotPresent inserts an item, and puts it in the queue. If the item is already\\n362: // present in the set, it is neither enqueued nor added to the set.\\n363: //\\n364: // This is useful in a single producer/consumer scenario so that the consumer can\\n365: // safely retry items without contending with the producer and potentially enqueueing\\n366: // stale items.\\n367: //\\n368: // Important: obj must be a Deltas (the output of the Pop() function). Yes, this is\\n369: // different from the Add/Update/Delete functions.\\n370: func (f *DeltaFIFO) AddIfNotPresent(obj interface{}) error {\\n371: \\tdeltas, ok := obj.(Deltas)\\n372: \\tif !ok {\\n373: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"object must be of type deltas, but got: %#v\\\", obj)\\n374: \\t}\\n375: \\tid, err := f.KeyOf(deltas)\\n376: \\tif err != nil {\\n377: \\t\\treturn KeyError{obj, err}\\n378: \\t}\\n379: \\tf.lock.Lock()\\n380: \\tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\\n381: \\tf.addIfNotPresent(id, deltas)\\n382: \\treturn nil\\n383: }\\n384: \\n385: // addIfNotPresent inserts deltas under id if it does not exist, and assumes the caller\\n386: // already holds the fifo lock.\\n387: func (f *DeltaFIFO) addIfNotPresent(id string, deltas Deltas) {\\n388: \\tf.populated = true\\n389: \\tif _, exists := f.items[id]; exists {\\n390: \\t\\treturn\\n391: \\t}\\n392: \\n393: \\tf.queue = append(f.queue, id)\\n394: \\tf.items[id] = deltas\\n395: \\tf.cond.Broadcast()\\n396: }\\n397: \\n398: // re-listing and watching can deliver the same update multiple times in any\\n399: // order. This will combine the most recent two deltas if they are the same.\\n400: func dedupDeltas(deltas Deltas) Deltas {\\n401: \\tn := len(deltas)\\n402: \\tif n < 2 {\\n403: \\t\\treturn deltas\\n404: \\t}\\n405: \\ta := &deltas[n-1]\\n406: \\tb := &deltas[n-2]\\n407: \\tif out := isDup(a, b); out != nil {\\n408: \\t\\tdeltas[n-2] = *out\\n409: \\t\\treturn deltas[:n-1]\\n410: \\t}\\n411: \\treturn deltas\\n412: }\\n413: \\n414: // If a & b represent the same event, returns the delta that ought to be kept.\\n415: // Otherwise, returns nil.\\n416: // TODO: is there anything other than deletions that need deduping?\\n417: func isDup(a, b *Delta) *Delta {\\n418: \\tif out := isDeletionDup(a, b); out != nil {\\n419: \\t\\treturn out\\n420: \\t}\\n421: \\t// TODO: Detect other duplicate situations? Are there any?\\n422: \\treturn nil\\n423: }\\n424: \\n425: // keep the one with the most information if both are deletions.\\n426: func isDeletionDup(a, b *Delta) *Delta {\\n427: \\tif b.Type != Deleted || a.Type != Deleted {\\n428: \\t\\treturn nil\\n429: \\t}\\n430: \\t// Do more sophisticated checks, or is this sufficient?\\n431: \\tif _, ok := b.Object.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\\n432: \\t\\treturn a\\n433: \\t}\\n434: \\treturn b\\n435: }\\n436: \\n437: // queueActionLocked appends to the delta list for the object.\\n438: // Caller must lock first.\\n439: func (f *DeltaFIFO) queueActionLocked(actionType DeltaType, obj interface{}) error {\\n440: \\treturn f.queueActionInternalLocked(actionType, actionType, obj)\\n441: }\\n442: \\n443: // function and must\\n446: // ignore emitDeltaTypeReplaced.\\n447: // Caller must lock first.\\n448: func (f *DeltaFIFO) queueActionInternalLocked(actionType, internalActionType DeltaType, obj so this is a good\\n455: \\t// place to call the transform func.\\n456: \\t//\\n457: \\t// If obj is a DeletedFinalStateUnknown tombstone or the action is a Sync,\\n458: \\t// then the object have already gone through the transformer.\\n459: \\t//\\n460: \\t// If the objects already present in the cache are passed to Replace(),\\n461: \\t// the transformer must be idempotent to avoid re-mutating them,\\n462: \\t// or coordinate with all readers from the cache to avoid data races.\\n463: \\t// Default informers do not pass existing objects to Replace.\\n464: \\tif f.transformer != {\\n490: \\t\\t\\tklog.Errorf(\\\"Impossible dedupDeltas for id=%q: oldDeltas=%#+v, obj=%#+v; ignoring\\\", id, oldDeltas, obj)\\n491: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n492: \\t\\t}\\n493: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/sets\"\n26: \n27: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n28: \tutiltrace \"k8s.io/utils/trace\"\n29: )\n30: \n31: // DeltaFIFOOptions is the configuration parameters for DeltaFIFO. All are\n32: // optional.\n33: type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\n34: \n35: \t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\n36: \t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\n37: \t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\n38: \t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n39: \tKeyFunction KeyFunc\n40: \n41: \t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\n42: \t// this queue \"knows about\". It is used to decide which items are missing\n43: \t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\n44: \t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\n45: \tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\n46: \n47: \t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\n48: \t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\n49: \t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\n50: \t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\n51: \t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\n52: \t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\n53: \tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n54: \n55: \t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\n56: \t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\n57: \tTransformer TransformFunc\n58: }\n59: \n60: // DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n69: //\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n74: // resync events.\n75: //\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n78: // the Pop() method.\n79: //\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n86: //\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\n90: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\n91: //\n92: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\n93: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\n94: // question are called \"known objects\" and this set of objects\n95: // modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\n96: // (each in a different way).\n97: //\n98: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\n99: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\n100: // different versions of the same object.\n101: type DeltaFIFO struct {\n102: \t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\n103: \tlock sync.RWMutex\n104: \tcond sync.Cond\n105: \n106: \t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\n107: \t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\n108: \titems map[string]Deltas\n109: \n110: \t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\n111: \t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\n112: \t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\n113: \tqueue []string\n114: \n115: \t// populated is true if the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has been populated\n116: \t// or Delete/Add/Update/AddIfNotPresent was called first.\n117: \tpopulated bool\n118: \t// initialPopulationCount is the number of items inserted by the first call of Replace()\n119: \tinitialPopulationCount int\n120: \n121: \t// keyFunc is used to make the key used for queued item\n122: \t// insertion and retrieval, and should be deterministic.\n123: \tkeyFunc KeyFunc\n124: \n125: \t// knownObjects list keys that are \"known\" --- affecting Delete(),\n126: \t// Replace(), and Resync()\n127: \tknownObjects KeyListerGetter\n128: \n129: \t// Used to indicate a queue is closed so a control loop can exit when a queue is empty.\n130: \t// Currently, not used to gate any of CRUD operations.\n131: \tclosed bool\n132: \n133: \t// emitDeltaTypeReplaced is whether to emit the Replaced or Sync\n134: \t// DeltaType when Replace() is called (to preserve backwards compat).\n135: \temitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n136: \n137: \t// Called with every object if non-nil.\n138: \ttransformer TransformFunc\n139: }\n140: \n141: // TransformFunc allows for transforming an object before it will be processed.\n142: //\n143: // The most common usage pattern is to clean-up some parts of the object to\n144: // reduce component memory usage if a given component doesn't care about them.\n145: //\n146: // New in v1.27: TransformFunc sees the object before any other actor, and it\n147: // is now safe to mutate the object in place instead of making a copy.\n148: //\n149: // It's recommended for the TransformFunc to be idempotent.\n150: // It MUST be idempotent if objects already present in the cache are passed to\n151: // the Replace() to avoid re-mutating them. Default informers do not pass\n152: // existing objects to Replace though.\n153: //\n154: // Note that TransformFunc is called while inserting objects into the\n155: // notification queue and is therefore extremely performance sensitive; please\n156: // do not do anything that will take a long time.\n157: type TransformFunc func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)\n158: \n159: // DeltaType is the type of a change (addition, deletion, etc)\n160: type DeltaType string\n161: \n162: // Change type definition\n163: const (\n164: \tAdded   DeltaType = \"Added\"\n165: \tUpdated DeltaType = \"Updated\"\n166: \tDeleted DeltaType = \"Deleted\"\n167: \t// Replaced is emitted when we encountered watch errors and had to do a\n168: \t// relist. We don't know if the replaced object has changed.\n169: \t//\n170: \t// NOTE: Previous versions of DeltaFIFO would use Sync for Replace events\n171: \t// as well. Hence, Replaced is only emitted when the option\n172: \t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is true.\n173: \tReplaced DeltaType = \"Replaced\"\n174: \t// Sync is for synthetic events during a periodic resync.\n175: \tSync DeltaType = \"Sync\"\n176: )\n177: \n178: // Delta is a member of Deltas (a list of Delta objects) which\n179: // in its turn is the type stored by a DeltaFIFO. It tells you what\n180: // change happened, and the object's state after* that change.\n181: //\n182: // [*] Unless the change is a deletion, and then you'll get the final\n183: // state of the object before it was deleted.\n184: type Delta struct {\n185: \tType   DeltaType\n186: \tObject interface{}\n187: }\n188: \n189: // Deltas is a list of one or more 'Delta's to an individual object.\n190: // The oldest delta is at index 0, the newest delta is the last one.\n191: type Deltas []Delta\n192: \n193: // NewDeltaFIFO returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to items.\n194: //\n195: // keyFunc is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It is\n196: // exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional handling\n197: // around deleted objects and queue state).\n198: //\n199: // 'knownObjects' may be supplied to modify the behavior of Delete,\n200: // Replace, and Resync.  It may be nil if you do not need those\n201: // modifications.\n202: //\n203: // TODO: consider merging keyLister with this object, tracking a list of\n204: // \"known\" keys when Pop() is called. Have to think about how that\n205: // affects error retrying.\n206: //\n207: //\tNOTE: It is possible to misuse this and cause a race when using an\n208: //\texternal known object source.\n209: //\tWhether there is a potential race depends on how the consumer\n210: //\tmodifies knownObjects. In Pop(), process function is called under\n211: //\tlock, so it is safe to update data structures in it that need to be\n212: //\tin sync with the queue (e.g. knownObjects).\n213: //\n214: //\tExample:\n215: //\tIn case of sharedIndexInformer being a consumer\n216: //\t(https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/0cdd940f/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go#L192),\n217: //\tthere is no race as knownObjects (s.indexer) is modified safely\n218: //\tunder DeltaFIFO's lock. The only exceptions are GetStore() and\n219: //\tGetIndexer() methods, which expose ways to modify the underlying\n220: //\tstorage. Currently these two methods are used for creating Lister\n221: //\tand internal tests.\n222: //\n223: // Also see the comment on DeltaFIFO.\n224: //\n225: // Warning: This constructs a DeltaFIFO that does not differentiate between\n226: // events caused by a call to Replace (e.g., from a relist, which may\n227: // contain object updates), and synthetic events caused by a periodic resync\n228: // (which just emit the existing object). See https://issue.k8s.io/86015 for details.\n229: //\n230: // Use `NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{..., EmitDeltaTypeReplaced: true})`\n231: // instead to receive a `Replaced` event depending on the type.\n232: //\n233: // Deprecated: Equivalent to NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{KeyFunction: keyFunc, KnownObjects: knownObjects})\n234: func NewDeltaFIFO(keyFunc KeyFunc, knownObjects KeyListerGetter) *DeltaFIFO {\n235: \treturn NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{\n236: \t\tKeyFunction:  keyFunc,\n237: \t\tKnownObjects: knownObjects,\n238: \t})\n239: }\n240: \n241: // NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to\n242: // items. See also the comment on DeltaFIFO.\n243: func NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(opts DeltaFIFOOptions) *DeltaFIFO {\n244: \tif opts.KeyFunction == nil {\n245: \t\topts.KeyFunction = MetaNamespaceKeyFunc\n246: \t}\n247: \n248: \tf := &DeltaFIFO{\n249: \t\titems:        map[string]Deltas{},\n250: \t\tqueue:        []string{},\n251: \t\tkeyFunc:      opts.KeyFunction,\n252: \t\tknownObjects: opts.KnownObjects,\n253: \n254: \t\temitDeltaTypeReplaced: opts.EmitDeltaTypeReplaced,\n255: \t\ttransformer:           opts.Transformer,\n256: \t}\n257: \tf.cond.L = &f.lock\n258: \treturn f\n259: }\n260: \n261: var (\n262: \t_ = Queue(&DeltaFIFO{}) // DeltaFIFO is a Queue\n263: )\n264: \n265: var (\n266: \t// ErrZeroLengthDeltasObject is returned in a KeyError if a Deltas\n267: \t// object with zero length is encountered (should be impossible,\n268: \t// but included for completeness).\n269: \tErrZeroLengthDeltasObject = errors.New(\"0 length Deltas object; can't get key\")\n270: )\n271: \n272: // Close the queue.\n273: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Close() {\n274: \tf.lock.Lock()\n275: \tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\n276: \tf.closed = true\n277: \tf.cond.Broadcast()\n278: }\n279: \n280: // KeyOf exposes f's keyFunc, but also detects the key of a Deltas object or\n281: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects.\n282: func (f *DeltaFIFO) KeyOf(obj interface{}) (string, error) {\n283: \tif d, ok := obj.(Deltas); ok {\n284: \t\tif len(d) == 0 {\n285: \t\t\treturn \"\", KeyError{obj, ErrZeroLengthDeltasObject}\n286: \t\t}\n287: \t\tobj = d.Newest().Object\n288: \t}\n289: \tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n290: \t\treturn d.Key, nil\n291: \t}\n292: \treturn f.keyFunc(obj)\n293: }\n294: \n295: // HasSynced returns true if an Add/Update/Delete/AddIfNotPresent are called first,\n296: // or the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has been popped.\n297: func (f *DeltaFIFO) HasSynced() bool {\n298: \tf.lock.Lock()\n299: \tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\n300: \treturn f.hasSynced_locked()\n301: }\n302: \n303: func (f *DeltaFIFO) hasSynced_locked() bool {\n304: \treturn f.populated && f.initialPopulationCount == 0\n305: }\n306: \n307: // Add inserts an item, and puts it in the queue. The item is only enqueued\n308: // if it doesn't already exist in the set.\n309: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Add(obj interface{}) error {\n310: \tf.lock.Lock()\n311: \tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\n312: \tf.populated = true\n313: \treturn f.queueActionLocked(Added, obj)\n314: }\n315: \n316: // Update is just like Add, but makes an Updated Delta.\n317: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Update(obj interface{}) error {\n318: \tf.lock.Lock()\n319: \tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\n320: \tf.populated = true\n321: \treturn f.queueActionLocked(Updated, obj)\n322: }\n323: \n324: // Delete is just like Add, but makes a Deleted Delta. If the given\n325: // object does not already exist, it will be ignored. (It may have\n326: // already been deleted by a Replace (re-list), for example.)  In this\n327: // method `f.knownObjects`, if not nil, provides (via GetByKey)\n328: // _additional_ objects that are considered to already exist.\n329: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Delete(obj interface{}) error {\n330: \tid, err := f.KeyOf(obj)\n331: \tif err != nil {\n332: \t\treturn KeyError{obj, err}\n333: \t}\n334: \tf.lock.Lock()\n335: \tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\n336: \tf.populated = true\n337: \tif f.knownObjects == nil {\n338: \t\tif _, exists := f.items[id]; !exists {\n339: \t\t\t// Presumably, this was deleted when a relist happened.\n340: \t\t\t// Don't provide a second report of the same deletion.\n341: \t\t\treturn nil\n342: \t\t}\n343: \t} else {\n344: \t\t// We only want to skip the \"deletion\" action if the object doesn't\n345: \t\t// exist in knownObjects and it doesn't have corresponding item in items.\n346: \t\t// Note that even if there is a \"deletion\" action in items, we can ignore it,\n347: \t\t// because it will be deduped automatically in \"queueActionLocked\"\n348: \t\t_, exists, err := f.knownObjects.GetByKey(id)\n349: \t\t_, itemsExist := f.items[id]\n350: \t\tif err == nil && !exists && !itemsExist {\n351: \t\t\t// Presumably, this was deleted when a relist happened.\n352: \t\t\t// Don't provide a second report of the same deletion.\n353: \t\t\treturn nil\n354: \t\t}\n355: \t}\n356: \n357: \t// exist in items and/or KnownObjects\n358: \treturn f.queueActionLocked(Deleted, obj)\n359: }\n360: \n361: // AddIfNotPresent inserts an item, and puts it in the queue. An `Indexer` for the local cache (allows efficient lookups)\\n2. A `Controller` that manages the reflector and processes queue items\\n3. A `sharedProcessor` that distributes notifications to registered event handlers\\n\\n## List-Watch Mechanism\\nThe list-watch pattern is implemented across two key files:\\n\\n### ListerWatcher Interface (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/listwatch.go`)\\nDefines the minimal interface for initial list and watch operations. The `ListWatch` struct provides concrete implementation with `NewListWatchFromClient()` factory that creates a ListerWatcher by binding to a Kubernetes REST client.\\n\\n### Reflector (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go`)\\nThe Reflector is the producer component that:\\n- Performs initial LIST operations to populate the cache with all existing objects\\n- Establishes a WATCH connection to receive real-time updates\\n- Implements exponential backoff for connection failures\\n- Periodically issues full LIST operations (resyncs) to detect missed updates\\n- Pushes all changes into the DeltaFIFO queue\\n- Provides `LastSyncResourceVersion()` to track the API server state\\n\\n## Local Cache Store Sync\\nThe local cache is implemented through a layered approach in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/`:\\n\\n### Store (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/store.go`)\\nBasic key-value store interface and implementation:\\n- `NewStore()` creates a simple cache backed by a ThreadSafeStore\\n- Supports Add, Update, Delete, Get, List operations\\n- Uses `DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc` as key function (namespace/name format)\\n\\n### Indexer (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/index.go`)\\nExtends Store with indexing capability:\\n- `NewIndexer()` wraps ThreadSafeStore with configurable index functions\\n- Allows efficient filtering by field or label selectors\\n- Maintains multiple indices for complex queries\\n\\n### ThreadSafeStore (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`)\\nUnderlying thread-safe storage:\\n- Protects all cache operations with RWMutex locks\\n- Maintains both item storage and multiple indices\\n- Implements atomic updates\\n\\n## Control Loop and Delta Processing\\nThe `Controller` in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/controller.go` (lines 96-206) orchestrates the flow:\\n1. Creates a Reflector with the ListerWatcher\\n2. Runs Reflector in a goroutine to feed the DeltaFIFO queue\\n3. `processLoop()` continuously pops items from the DeltaFIFO and processes them\\n4. `processDeltas()` updates the local cache and invokes registered handlers\\n\\n## Delta FIFO Queue\\nThe `DeltaFIFO` in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` (lines 60-178) is the critical queue implementation:\\n- Tracks changes as `Deltas` - sequences of state changes (Added, Updated, Deleted, Sync, Replaced)\\n- Deduplicates consecutive identical operations\\n- Maintains FIFO ordering for processing\\n- Integrates with the local cache (\\\"knownObjects\\\") to generate synthetic Deleted deltas when objects disappear\\n- Supports periodic resync operations to detect missed updates\\n- Pop() operations are blocking, allowing the consumer to process one item at a time\\n\\n## Event Distribution\\nOnce items are processed by the controller and the local cache is updated, the `sharedProcessor` and `processorListener` components (in shared_informer.go, lines 705-991) distribute notifications to event handlers:\\n- Multiple event handlers can be registered on a single informer\\n- Handlers receive OnAdd, OnUpdate, OnDelete callbacks\\n- Notifications include an `isInInitialList` flag to distinguish initial sync from live updates\\n- A ring buffer prevents slow handlers from blocking others\\n- Resync events periodically replay all cached objects to handlers that request them\\n\\n## Synchronization and Starting\\nThe `Start()` method in the factory (lines 143-165) initiates the entire pipeline:\\n1. Starts all registered informers in parallel goroutines\\n2. Each informer's Run() method starts its controller\\n3. The controller starts the reflector and begins the process loop\\n4. `WaitForCacheSync()` polls all informers' `HasSynced()` methods until they return true\\n5. Once synced, the local cache contains all objects from the API server\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that all components in Kubernetes that need to watch API resources can efficiently maintain a local cache in sync with the API server, with minimal network overhead and strong consistency guarantees.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5330,"cache_read_input_tokens":102400,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":5330},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e5789629-9620-4451-a860-ca02437000dd","uuid":"a455f5e6-af01-40fb-85bc-6e345008dc4c"}
